The Circumstances of Yu Youren's Trip South 92

The Guangdong Authorities Try to Retain Hu, but Hu Does Not Immediately Go to Nanjing

Yu Arrives in Guangdong Solely to Commemorate the Seventy-Two Martyrs

Guangzhou Correspondence: On this occasion of Mr. Yu Youren's trip south, his initial purpose upon arriving in Hong Kong was to persuade Hu Hanmin, who was living in seclusion on the island, to prepare for a trip to Nanjing. Before Mr. Yu arrived in Hong Kong, Xiao Focheng and Lin Zhong from Guangdong also arrived in Hong Kong to discuss important matters with Mr. Hu. They had dinner at Mr. Hu's residence on the evening of the 15th, discussing the current situation until about 9 p.m. On the 16th, Mr. Yu Youren drove from his hotel to visit Mr. Hu. After talking for about an hour, Zhang Huichang, who was also traveling south, also visited Mr. Hu. Mr. Hu did not immediately agree to Mr. Yu's earnest request to go north. On the afternoon of the 16th, Xiao Focheng, Lin Jizhong, and Wu Chaoshu from Guangdong jointly visited Mr. Hu at his private residence and discussed matters for a long time. It is said that the outcome was that the three organizations in Guangdong (i.e., the Southwest Executive Department, the Military Commission, and the Political Committee) must be protected, no matter how their names are changed, in order to implement the spirit of balanced power. As for Mr. Hu Hanmin's attitude, he also decided not to go to Nanjing. On the 17th, Mr. Hu publicly issued a statement, saying that his blood pressure was still high, he had been worried and overworked recently, and he was often dizzy. He was so weak that he could not travel north in fact. People generally worry that no one in the central government will take responsibility if Chiang, Wang, and Hu do not enter the capital, but this is a big mistake. The current government system takes the Executive Yuan as the highest organ for exercising governance, and the Executive Yuan is only responsible to the Central Political Council, not to the Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee. All major plans are decided by all members of the Central Political Council. The so-called Standing Committee is only responsible for taking turns presiding over the meetings of the Central Political Council. Now that the national crisis is imminent, resisting insults should be the priority. Being busy sending someone off and welcoming someone else, focusing on the person rather than the matter, is a mistake. The central government should set up a special committee to preside over everything, with central guidance from above. Therefore, whether the Standing Committee members go to Beijing is not a problem. The urgent task at present is to recover lost territory externally and suppress bandits and communists internally. He hopes that the current central government will implement revolutionary policies in the spirit of a responsible cabinet. Although he is sick, he will do his best to support it, etc. Seeing that Mr. Hu had already expressed his opinions, Mr. Yu Youren did not want to force him to go north again, so he came to Guangdong to visit the members of the Central Executive Committee in Guangdong and invite them to go north together to face the national crisis. The Guangdong authorities also sent Miao Peinan to Hong Kong to welcome Mr. Yu. Mr. Yu then took the Guangzhou-Kowloon express train to Guangdong on the afternoon of the 18th and arrived in Guangzhou at about 7 p.m. Chen Jitang, Bai Chongxi, Liu Jiwen, and people from the military, government, and party circles all went to the station to welcome him. That evening, Mr. Yu temporarily stayed at the Central Hotel in Xidi. Those traveling with him included Central Executive Committee member Wang Luyi and Yu's secretary Liu Kaizhong. The next day (the 18th), Mr. Yu felt that the national crisis was imminent and the country's affairs had not yet been settled. Stepping on the land of Guangdong, he remembered the martyrs and could not help but sigh. So at about 10 a.m., he went to Huanghuagang to commemorate the seventy-two martyrs, lingering and sighing for a long time before leaving. In the afternoon, he went to Zhixin School to visit and also visited Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall and the museum. At about 3 p.m., at the invitation of the authorities, he moved to Tuisi Garden in Dongshan. Mr. Yu, in view of Hu Hanmin's failure to go north, did not express his southern mission in his conversations with people, only saying that he came to Guangdong to meet Guangzhou friends whom he had not seen for many years and to visit the famous revolutionary base, and that he would return north after staying for two or three days. On the 19th, Xiao Focheng and Lin Jizhong, who went to Hong Kong to discuss the current situation with Hu Hanmin, returned to Guangdong and went back with Wu Chaoshu. At 11 a.m. that morning, Chen Jitang, Bai Chongxi, and Liu Jiwen held a banquet at Tuisi Garden to welcome Mr. Yu Youren and Mr. Wu Chaoshu. Xiao Focheng, Lin Yizhong, and dozens of army commanders were also present. During the banquet, the people of Guangdong expressed the following opinions: (1) Because Mr. Hu ZhanTang's blood pressure is still over 170, it is indeed difficult for him to travel far. Please ask him to go north when his spirits recover. (2) The three southwestern organizations were established based on the resolutions of the Fourth Plenary Session. Please ask Committee Member Yu to explain to the committees in Beijing when he returns north. (3) Regarding the reorganization of southwestern politics, the committees asked Wu Chaoshu to take the position of Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government as soon as possible. (4) The committees also expressed their opinions on the southwestern border issues. They dispersed at 3 p.m. (January 20th)

Zhang Fakui's Troops Depart to Aid Heilongjiang 93

With the Actual Strength of One Division Under Wu Qiwai

Started from Yongzhou on the 4th of this Month

Guangzhou Correspondence: Zhang Fakui's Fourth Army stationed in Guangxi had previously telegraphed the authorities for permission to depart to aid Heilongjiang. The Guangxi authorities initially considered that the southwest border defense was also important. For the sake of careful consideration, they ordered the troops to postpone their departure from Guangxi. Later, because Zhang Fakui strongly requested to fight for the country and his troops were particularly determined to eliminate the enemy, the headquarters of the Fourth Army Group approved the departure of the troops. However, the Guangxi Army Huang Heling Division (the Tenth Division), which was usually under Zhang's command, could not accompany them due to the importance of southwest national defense. Huang's troops have been ordered by the Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Army Group to go to Longzhou to handle pacification matters. Therefore, Zhang Fakui's troops are actually only the Eleventh Division under Wu Qiwai. (Zhang's army suffered great losses due to repeated battles. Since fighting with the 19th Route Army in Hengyang the year before last, it only had one division's strength left after returning to Guangxi.) On the 27th of last month, Wu's division held a meeting to prepare for departure and decided on the steps to take. On the first of this month, a swearing-in ceremony was held in Nanning. Ye Qi, Chief of Staff of the Fourth Army Group, and other officers were present to observe. Ye Qi, in his capacity as Chief of Staff and on behalf of the Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Army Group, gave a speech to all the officers and soldiers of Wu's troops. On the 4th, Wu's troops, led by Deputy Division Commander Han Pingyi, departed. All the groups in Nanning sent representatives to the North Gate to send them off. Wu's troops followed the road north and passed Binyang on the 6th, Qianjiang on the 7th, Liuzhou on the 14th, took the road to Pingle, and arrived at Quanzhou on the 20th, heading towards southern Hunan. It is said that the troops have obtained He Jian's consent to allow them to pass through Hunan. It is said that they will arrive in Nanjing on February 5th. (January 21st)

League of Nations Water Conservancy Experts Arrive in Bengbu 94

To Inspect the Huai River, the Abandoned Yellow River, and the Grand Canal

Bengbu Correspondence: Mr. Haas, the Minister of Transportation of the League of Nations from England, and others were invited by our government to come to China to study various issues in China. They have made considerable contributions to various construction projects. Haas is particularly concerned about our country's transportation and water conservancy projects. Last March, he came to Bengbu for a time to investigate the situation of the Huai River. After returning to Beijing, he submitted a general report to the Huai River Guidance Committee, believing that it was a contribution to the implementation of Huai River guidance. Now the National Government has again invited Haas and four transportation and water conservancy experts from the Transportation Department of the League of Nations to investigate the situation of the Shanghai Port, the Huangpu River, Jiangsu, Anhui, the Huai River, and the Tianjin Hai River in order to prepare for the implementation of construction and dredging. The Huai River Guidance Committee specially translated the Huai River guidance plan into English and handed it over to Haas and others for review and suggestions in order to implement the Huai River guidance project in the future. Recently, the National Government invited Haas and others to go north to inspect the situation of the Huai River, the abandoned Yellow River, and the Grand Canal, and sent Cao Boquan, a representative of the National Economic Council, and Xu Junti, Deputy Chief Engineer of the Huai River Guidance Committee, to accompany and entertain them. The Twelfth District Labor Relief Bureau and the Changhuai River Water Police Bureau here have all received telegrams to prepare everything. They have found a transportation villa as a reception center. Wang Huzhen, Director of the Labor Relief Bureau, received a telegram from Beijing a few days ago, saying that the League of Nations experts were expected to arrive on the morning of the 23rd, so yesterday (the 22nd) at 1 p.m., he invited representatives from various organizations and groups to the third floor of the transportation villa to discuss reception and protection matters. It was decided that the Bengbu Public Security Bureau, the Water Police Bureau, the Military Police Supervision Office, and the 47th Army Division would be responsible for reception and protection. Today (the 23rd) at 2 p.m., the military police forces were deployed separately. The Military Police Supervision Office, the Public Security Bureau, and the Water Police Bureau were responsible for guarding the reception center (i.e., the transportation villa). A company of the 47th Division was responsible for guarding the area from Erma Road to Dama Road Station. The Public Security Bureau's security team was on guard at the station. Those who arrived at the station to welcome them included Shen Yuanzhen, Director of the Military Police Supervision Office, Zhao Chunpu, Director of the Bengbu Public Security Bureau, Lu Fengshu, Director of the Water Police Bureau, Wang Huzhen, Director of the Twelfth Labor Relief Bureau, and Gao Weixuan, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. At 3:40 p.m., the experts took the second train into the station. The security team paid their respects. Haas, the Minister of Transportation of the League of Nations, was unable to come due to his recent appointment as Secretary-General of the League of Nations Investigation Team, his busy affairs, and his slight indisposition. Those who arrived were Englishman Gaode, Frenchman Berliaux, German Sivikin, and Dutchman Budley. The National Government also sent Cao and Xu, two specialists, to accompany them. After the four foreigners got off the train, Wang Huzhen introduced them to the crowd through a translator. They then went out of the station together and took a car to the third floor of the transportation villa to rest. It is said that they are scheduled to depart from Bengbu tomorrow morning (the 24th) to survey the Huai River. The Water Police Bureau has prepared a large Yuda steamboat and sent thirty to forty water police officers on the Chang'an warship, along with sixty armed soldiers from the 47th Division, to protect them. The Anhui Northern Suppression Headquarters has also telegraphed the counties along the Huai River to provide additional protection when the experts arrive. It is said that the four experts are planning to sail up the river first, pass through Huaiyuan and arrive at Fengtai for a day of inspection, spend the night on the road, and then return to Bengbu and sail down to Wuhe and the Hongze Lake to Jiangba to inspect the river shape, waterway, transportation, water disaster, and the achievements of labor relief and dike construction. From Jiangba, they will take a car to Huaiyin to inspect the abandoned Yellow River, then go south along the Grand Canal to inspect the Grand Canal project, and return to Beijing from Zhenjiang to report. The inspection is scheduled to be completed in two weeks. During the inspection period, all travel expenses will be borne by the National Government. (January 23rd)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 95

The Debate on the Caojing Election Case Concludes. The Caojing District Office previously handled the election of township heads and there were some disputes among the voters. The district reported to the county government and sent a letter to the court for verification. The defendant was Chen Maosheng, who was accused of disrupting the election and obstructing official duties. After the prosecutor's office summoned and interrogated the results, the charge of disrupting the election was dismissed, and the charge of obstructing official duties was prosecuted under Article 142, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. The criminal court held a hearing today, first questioning witnesses Bao Haiping and others, and then questioning the defendant Chen Maosheng, who stated the circumstances and proved that there was no obstruction of official duties. The judge announced the end of the debate and set the verdict for Saturday.

Suzhou 96

The High Court Executes a Criminal. Zhou Awu, a tea room employee of the Shanghai Wuhua Road Refining Company, a native of Dongshan, Dongting, was 37 years old. He was in charge of the front and back door locks of the company. On January 3rd of last year, he colluded with four unknown people and apprentice Shi Ruijing to chop the accountant Xu Kuijun to death with an axe and steal more than 3,400 yuan of silver dollars from the iron box. Later, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau arrested and sent him to the local court, where he and Shi Ruijing were sentenced to death. Shi and others refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the High Court, which changed Shi's sentence to five years in prison, while Zhou's death sentence was upheld. Yesterday (the 26th) at 8 a.m., Prosecutor Sun Xiyan from the High Procuratorate escorted Zhou to Wangshudun outside Yanmen and executed him by shooting.

Changshu 97

The Farmer Shooting Case May Be Resolved. When Wang Hongyu, the former head of the tenth district of this county, was in office, farmers rioted due to famine and the police suppressed them improperly, resulting in the shooting of four farmers. Subsequently, the villagers in the district accused Wang of ordering the shooting and filed a complaint with the provincial government and the High Court. As a result, Wang was dismissed from his post. After the Wuxian District Court investigated the case once, Wang Hongyu and the police squad leader Jin Dingxun were detained. Later, the prosecutor did not prosecute Wang for one part of the case and allowed him to be released on bail. As for squad leader Jin, he had admitted to ordering the shooting, so he was prosecuted. The court held another hearing the day before yesterday, but the plaintiff Shen Zhongshan and the families of the deceased did not appear in court. It is said that the case has been mediated and the plaintiff has agreed, but they must request compensation for the families of the deceased. The defendant is also very willing, so this case is expected to be resolved peacefully.

Fishing Boat Outside Hupu Port Engages in Fierce Battle with Bandit Ship. Hupu Town in this county is located on the riverside and is an important town in our county. It mainly exports bean cakes, fish, and shrimp. Recently, the fishing industry has become more developed. There are often merchant ships from Dalian, Shandong and other places coming and going, but bandits are rampant in the river and merchant ships do not dare to travel alone. Whenever there are exports, they often travel in groups. The other day, the Jinfulong boat from Hupu Town loaded goods in Dalian and arrived in Shanghai. After unloading, it sailed back to Hupu from Wusongkou. Unexpectedly, when passing the Jiangmian area of ​​Sheshan Weng, a small ship suddenly came opposite. Seeing that the people on the ship were carrying guns and other weapons, they knew they had encountered bandits. The crew of the ship used the ship's own guns to load bullets and prepare, while still sailing forward. The pirate ship had fifty or sixty pirates. Knowing that the other party was prepared, they immediately fired their guns. The crew of the ship saw them firing and immediately fired back. The sound of gunfire filled the river for about half an hour. Two of the crew members were shot and injured. Seeing that they were outnumbered and running out of ammunition, they had to retreat. However, the bandit ship was still chasing closely. Fortunately, they were able to escape thanks to the favorable wind and tide. After the Jinfulong ship arrived in Hupu, it sent the two injured crew members to the Suzhou Boxi Hospital for treatment. It is said that the crew members were fortunately not shot in vital areas and there is no danger to their lives.

Wuxi 98

Communist Zhu Yongtai's Case Clarified as a False Accusation. Zhu Yongtai, a communist, was arrested the year before last and interrogated by the county government's temporary court, but no conclusion has been reached. Yesterday, Chen Shitao, a judge from the county court, re-examined the case and summoned Zhu A'er, the person who reported him, for questioning. After repeated questioning, it was discovered that Zhu Yongtai was not a communist. However, he was usually a rogue and had seduced a village girl, incurring the anger of the villagers, who then reported him for joining the Communist Party. Now that there is no solid evidence, the anti-revolutionary part of the case is not established and the verdict is scheduled to be announced on the 28th.

Bandits Rob and Shoot the Owner. Zhang A'er, a guest resident of Taoyuan Village, Kaiyuan Township, Fourth District of the county, was suddenly visited by more than a dozen bandits on the night of the day before yesterday. They each carried handguns and flashlights and broke into the house. At that time, the men and women of the Zhang family were all asleep. After the bandits entered the room, they immediately grabbed Zhang A'er and forced him to say where the silver was hidden. A'er's answer provoked the bandits' anger, and they pulled out their handguns and fired two shots at A'er's legs. A'er fell to the ground in extreme pain, unconscious. The bandits then ransacked the cabinets, looting on a large scale. After an hour, they left with their loot.

Nantong 99

A False Alarm Due to a Misunderstanding Between the Public Security Bureau and the Volunteer Corps. The Nantong Anti-Japanese Volunteer Corps was established under the guidance of Shi Zezhi, who was sent by the Nanjing General Corps. It held a meeting at the public lecture hall in the city at 9 p.m. on the 24th. The Public Security Bureau dispatched an armed police force to search and arrest them. For a time, the situation was tense and the shops in the city closed their doors and pedestrians ran to avoid them. The members of the corps went to the Public Security Bureau together, where Deputy Director Li explained the misunderstanding and expressed his apology. The members of the corps dispersed at 10:30 p.m.

The Pingchao Wu Yang Bandit Case Sentenced. The issue of jurisdiction over the Pingchao Wu Qinmian Yang JinYun bandit case caused a dispute between the administrative and judicial organs. After Wu and Yang were declared not guilty and released by the court, they were captured by the county government and handed over to the Suppression Military Law Office for trial. The verdict has now been made. Wu Qinmian was sentenced to four years in prison and Yang Jinyun was sentenced to two years in prison.

Zhenjiang 100

The Court Investigates the Wuchang Steamboat Opium Case. According to a report from Zhang Yiwu, an advisor to the 121st Brigade of the 61st Division stationed in Zhenjiang, the Wuchang steamboat was carrying a large amount of opium to Zhenjiang. Zhang was sent to lead a team to inspect the boat. A large amount of opium, about 13,000 taels, was found on the boat. Zhang only presented about 1,000 taels to the brigade headquarters and embezzled the rest. The court has now learned of this matter and has sent a letter to the brigade headquarters asking them to transfer the confiscated opium to the court for investigation and to severely investigate the matter.
